Secondly, I find the Floss Action better by a wide margin over any of the others I have tried. There are a few reasons why. First, it gets between large gaps in the teeth like no other replacement head. For example, I have a wide gap between two teeth caused by a dental root canal. This brush cleans in the space in a way the others don't. I do not have to worry about bad breathe from the root canal anymore! Secondly, it gets deeper into tight spaces as well. I have been told by multiple dental assistants it is very difficult to floss me because the teeth are located close together. With these heads there is no issue! Third, The brush is not too rough or soft. I have average teeth and gums in regards to sensitivity. It seems today everyone thinks they have soft or hard gums. Well you know what, most people are \\"average\\" - this is the very definition of average! This brush is intended for the 80-90% of us who have average gums and teeth. My teeth aren't left slimy from a too soft brush and my gums don't hurt from a too rough one. Finally, This head feels the best. You can tell by the unique oscillating rotations that this is a brush with unique features. It doesn't do in a circle like others. All the bristles move in awkward ways, creating a sensation that leaves me happy!

  236. So I've been using the Oral B Floss Action heads on my Oral B I've had for about 4 years now (still going strong!), and overall, I'll say I like it.<br /><br />First, the bristles are stiff, much stiffer than even the regular replacement heads. This may be a deal breaker for some, since stiff brushes have many negatives. While they seem to get your teeth cleaner, and quicker, they can damage gums, possibly enamel, so many dentists do not recommend stiff bristles.<br /><br />Second thing to note, this shouldn't be a flossing replacement. You'd think it'd go without saying, but no, no product really has proven itself to leave flossing completely unnecessary.<br /><br />Third, these are big, much bigger than the normal Oral B heads, and small teeth/mouths may not find these as functional.<br /><br />So, with that, you'd think these are the worst brushes in the world, right? Well, maybe not. For starters, with any of the Oral B automatic toothbrushes, you let the brush do the work, so you really shouldn't press this hard against your teeth like a normal toothbrush. I don't know if this completely eliminates any possible damage, but so far my gums/teeth feel fine, not beaten up, and doesn't feel radically different from using a medium bristle brush.<br /><br />These also do seem to do a better job of getting between your teeth clean, and in general getting the majority of your teeth clean.<br /><br />Finally, these heads seem to fit my teeth perfect, but I should note, I have a large mouth and large teeth. As such, they seem to do an excellent job for me, but I could see how they'd be less beneficial for smaller teeth/mouths.<br /><br />All in all, I got 3 of these heads pretty cheap, and they were a pretty good deal, but they may not be for everyone.
